| | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | |Is abortion leagal in India? MTP Act of 1971| | |Medagg| |Medagg| |<img class="" src="https://images.surferseo.art/4800d368-ab5f-4307-81b4-35ced94a728c.png" alt="Is abortion legal in India?" width="1271" height="715" data-pm-slice="0 1 []" />  Yes, abortion is legal in India, but only under certain circumstances. The Medical Termination of Pregnancy (MTP) Act of 1971 of India outlines the specific grounds under which abortion is permitted in the country. Under the MTP Act, abortion is allowed up to 20 weeks of gestational age based on the advice of one registered medical practitioner. For pregnancies between 20 and 24 weeks, abortion is permitted as an exception, but only under specific categories, such as cases of sexual assault, rape, or fetal abnormalities. These cases require the approval of two registered medical practitioners. After 24 weeks, the law mandates the formation of a medical board in approved facilities to determine if termination is allowed based on substantial fetal abnormality. However, the Supreme Court has granted permission for abortions beyond this period in certain exceptional cases, such as those involving minors or severe health risks to the pregnant woman. <h2>Is Abortion Legal in India for Unmarried Women?</h2> Yes, abortion is legal in India for unmarried women, but the grounds are slightly different compared to married women. For unmarried women, abortion is permitted under the same grounds as for married women, such as: <ul>  	<li>The continuance of the pregnancy would involve a risk to the life of the pregnant woman or of grave injury to her physical or mental health.</li>  	<li>There is a substantial risk that if the child were born, it would suffer from such physical or mental abnormalities as to be seriously handicapped.</li>  	<li>The pregnancy is caused by rape.</li>  	<li>The pregnancy is caused by failure of any contraceptive device or method used by a married woman or her partner.</li> </ul> However, the MTP Act does not explicitly mention unmarried women as a separate category. In practice, unmarried women may face additional barriers or scrutiny when seeking abortion services, as societal stigma and moral judgments can play a role. Ensuring access to abortion services for unmarried women is crucial for upholding their reproductive rights. <h2>How Much Does an Abortion Cost in India?</h2> The cost of an abortion in India can vary widely depending on several factors, such as: <ul>  	<li>The gestational age of the pregnancy</li>  	<li>The method of abortion (surgical or medical)</li>  	<li>The location and type of healthcare facility (private or public)</li>  	<li>The experience and qualifications of the healthcare provider</li> </ul> In general, the cost of an early surgical abortion (up to 12 weeks) in a public hospital can range from ₹1,000 to ₹5,000. In private clinics, the cost can range from ₹10,000 to ₹30,000 or more. The cost of a medical abortion (using abortion pills) can range from ₹1,500 to ₹5,000, depending on the location and healthcare provider. It’s important to note that the cost may also include additional expenses, such as pre-procedure consultations, diagnostic tests, and post-procedure follow-up care. <h2>How to Abort an Unplanned Pregnancy in India</h2> If you have an unplanned pregnancy in India and wish to terminate it, the first step is to consult a registered medical practitioner (RMP) who is qualified to perform abortions. Here are the general steps to abort an unplanned pregnancy in India: <ol>  	<li>Confirm the pregnancy and determine the gestational age.</li>  	<li>Consult an RMP and discuss the available options based on the gestational age and your specific circumstances. The gestational limit for abortion in India is 24 weeks, except in certain exceptional cases.</li>  	<li>If the RMP determines that your case falls under the grounds for legal abortion, they will provide you with the necessary information and guidance.</li>  	<li>Provide the required consent and any necessary documentation, such as proof of identity or guardian consent (if applicable).</li>  	<li>Undergo the abortion procedure, which can be either a surgical or medical abortion, depending on the gestational age and your preference.</li>  	<li>Follow the post-procedure instructions and attend any recommended follow-up appointments.</li> </ol> It’s important to note that abortion services should be sought from registered and reputable healthcare providers to ensure the safety and legality of the procedure. <h2><strong>Legal Consequences for Abortion in India</strong></h2> Abortion is legal in India, but only under specific circumstances outlined in the Medical Termination of Pregnancy (MTP) Act of 1971. Any unauthorized abortion performed by an unregistered medical practitioner is considered illegal and can lead to severe legal consequences: <ul>  	<li>Imprisonment of up to 7 years for the person performing the illegal abortion</li>  	<li>Imprisonment of up to 10 years if the abortion is done without the woman’s consent</li>  	<li>Fines and other legal penalties for the woman undergoing an illegal abortion</li> </ul> Performing an abortion outside the legal framework established by the MTP Act is considered illegal and can result in criminal penalties for both the pregnant woman and the healthcare provider.  The MTP Act strictly regulates who can perform abortions and where they can be conducted. Violating these regulations can result in criminal charges for both the provider and the woman seeking the abortion. <h2><strong>Evolution of the Medical Termination of Pregnancy Act</strong></h2> The MTP Act has undergone several amendments since its inception in 1971 to expand access to safe and legal abortion services in India: <ul>  	<li>1971: The original MTP Act allowed abortion up to 20 weeks of pregnancy under certain conditions.</li>  	<li>2021: The Act was amended by the to increase the upper gestational limit for abortion from 20 to 24 weeks in certain cases, such as fetal abnormalities or pregnancies resulting from sexual assault.</li>  	<li>2022: The Supreme Court ruled that the distinction between married and unmarried women in the MTP Act is unconstitutional, allowing all women access to safe and legal abortion up to 24 weeks.</li> </ul> These changes have aimed to make abortion more accessible and align India’s laws with global trends towards liberalizing abortion rights. These amendments reflect a growing recognition of the importance of reproductive healthcare in ensuring women's health and rights. <h2><strong>Criteria for Obtaining Abortion in India</strong></h2> Under the MTP Act, abortion is permitted in India if: <ul>  	<li>Continuing the pregnancy poses a risk to the woman’s life or causes grave injury to her physical or mental health.</li>  	<li>There is a substantial risk that the child would be born with severe physical or mental abnormalities.</li>  	<li>The pregnancy is a result of rape or contraceptive failure (for married women).</li> </ul> The gestational limit for abortion is 24 weeks, except in cases of fetal abnormalities or sexual assault, where it can be extended. Abortion can only be performed by a registered medical practitioner in a registered medical facility, and the woman’s consent is required. <h2><strong>Comparison to Other Countries</strong></h2> Compared to many other countries, India’s abortion laws are relatively progressive, though challenges remain in implementation and access. Some key points: <ul>  	<li>India allows abortion on broader grounds than many countries, including for mental health reasons and in cases of contraceptive failure.</li>  	<li>The recent Supreme Court ruling aligning abortion rights for married and unmarried women is a positive step, unlike in some countries where unmarried women face greater barriers.</li>  	<li>However, the 24-week gestational limit is still lower than in countries like the U.S. (pre-Dobbs) and Canada, which have no such limit.</li>  	<li>Unsafe abortions remain a concern in India due to social stigma, lack of awareness, and access barriers, unlike in countries with more robust reproductive healthcare systems.</li> </ul> <h2><strong>Psychological Impacts of Unsafe Abortions</strong></h2> Unsafe abortions, performed by unqualified providers or in unsanitary conditions, can have severe psychological and mental health consequences for women in India, including: <ul>  	<li>Trauma, anxiety, and depression from the unsafe procedure and potential complications</li>  	<li>Feelings of guilt, shame, and social stigma due to the legal and moral complexities around abortion</li>  	<li>Long-term mental health issues stemming from the physical and emotional toll of an unsafe abortion</li> </ul> Ensuring access to safe, legal, and stigma-free abortion services is crucial to protect women’s mental well-being and reproductive autonomy in India <h2><strong>Impact of Supreme Court Ruling on Unmarried Women Seeking Abortions</strong></h2> The recent Supreme Court ruling has had a significant impact on the rights of unmarried women to access safe and legal abortion services in India. The key points are: <ul>  	<li>The Supreme Court ruled that the distinction between married and unmarried women in the Medical Termination of Pregnancy (MTP) Act is unconstitutional.</li>  	<li>This means that all women, regardless of marital status, now have the same right to access abortion services up to 24 weeks of pregnancy.</li>  	<li>Prior to this ruling, the MTP Act only explicitly allowed married women to access abortion services between 20-24 weeks under certain conditions. Unmarried women were excluded from this provision.</li>  	<li>The court held that denying unmarried women the same abortion rights as married women would perpetuate stereotypes and violate their fundamental rights to reproductive autonomy and dignity.</li> </ul> <h2><strong>New Criteria for Obtaining Abortion Under 2021 MTP Amendment Act</strong></h2> The key criteria for obtaining an abortion in India under the 2021 MTP Amendment Act are: <ul>  	<li>Up to 20 weeks of pregnancy - Abortion can be performed based on the advice of one registered medical practitioner.</li>  	<li>20-24 weeks of pregnancy - Abortion can be performed based on the advice of two registered medical practitioners. This applies to cases involving: <ul>  	<li>Substantial fetal abnormalities</li>  	<li>Pregnancies resulting from sexual assault/rape (including marital rape)</li>  	<li>Change in the pregnant woman's material circumstances</li> </ul> </li> </ul> The Supreme Court ruling has now extended this 20-24 week provision to all women, regardless of marital status. <h2><strong>Consent Requirements for Married vs Unmarried Women</strong></h2> The consent requirements for abortion differ slightly between married and unmarried women: <ul>  	<li>Married women - Spousal consent is not required. Only the woman's consent is needed.</li>  	<li>Unmarried women - Parental/guardian consent is required if the woman is a minor (under 18 years). For adult unmarried women, only their own consent is required.</li> </ul> The Supreme Court ruling upheld that the woman's right to abortion is based on her personal autonomy, not dependent on marital status or familial consent. <h2><strong>Implications on Familial Consent</strong></h2> The Supreme Court's ruling has significant implications for the role of family members in a woman's decision to have an abortion: <ul>  	<li>The court emphasized that the decision to have an abortion rests solely with the pregnant woman, not her family.</li>  	<li>It rejected the idea that unmarried women need parental/spousal consent, stating this would violate their fundamental rights.</li>  	<li>The ruling makes it clear that healthcare providers cannot deny abortion services based on lack of family consent, as long as the woman herself consents.</li> </ul> This affirms the primacy of the woman's reproductive autonomy over familial or societal pressures. <h2><strong>Addressing Marital Rape and Abortion</strong></h2> An important aspect of the Supreme Court's ruling is its interpretation of "rape" under the MTP Act: <ul>  	<li>The court held that the definition of "rape" must include marital rape, solely for the purpose of accessing legal abortion services.</li>  	<li>This is significant as India does not currently criminalize marital rape under the Indian Penal Code.</li>  	<li>By including marital rape as grounds for abortion, the court has provided a legal avenue for women facing sexual violence within marriage to terminate unwanted pregnancies.</li> </ul> This ruling helps address a critical gap in India's abortion laws and recognizes the reality of intimate partner violence that many women face. <h2><strong>Legalities of Abortion in India: Additional FAQs</strong></h2> <h2><strong>1. Can a Married Woman Get an Abortion in India?</strong></h2> Yes, a married woman can get an abortion in India. The Medical Termination of Pregnancy (MTP) Act of 1971 allows for abortion under specific conditions, including contraceptive failure. The Act does not require spousal consent for the abortion procedure. <h2><strong>2. Can an Unmarried Woman Get an Abortion in India?</strong></h2> Yes, an unmarried woman can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act permits abortion under similar conditions as for married women, such as risk to physical or mental health, fetal abnormalities, and contraceptive failure. However, the consent of a parent or guardian is required if the woman is a minor. <h2><strong>3. What Are the Legal Consequences for Performing an Illegal Abortion in India?</strong></h2> Performing an illegal abortion in India can result in severe legal consequences. The MTP Act mandates that only registered medical practitioners can perform abortions, and unauthorized abortions are illegal. Penalties include imprisonment for up to 7 years for the person performing the abortion and up to 10 years if the abortion is performed without the woman's consent. <h2><strong>4. Can a Minor Girl Get an Abortion in India?</strong></h2> Yes, a minor girl can get an abortion in India. However, the written consent of her legal guardian is required. The MTP Act allows abortions under certain health-related grounds, which can include the case of a minor girl who is unlikely to be able to raise a child due to her age. <h2><strong>5. Does India Have a Law Against Marital Rape?</strong></h2> No, India does not have a specific law against marital rape. However, the MTP Act allows for abortion in cases of rape, including marital rape. This means that even if marital rape is not criminalized, a woman can still seek an abortion if her pregnancy is a result of rape. <h2><strong>6. Can a Woman Get an Abortion Without Her Family's Consent?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman can get an abortion without her family's consent. The MTP Act only requires the consent of the woman herself, and the consent of family members is not necessary. This ensures that the woman's autonomy and reproductive rights are protected. <h2><strong>7. Can a Woman Get an Abortion After 24 Weeks in India?</strong></h2> No, a woman cannot get an abortion after 24 weeks in India, except in specific cases where a medical board has approved the termination due to substantial fetal abnormalities. The MTP Act sets a 24-week limit for abortions, and only in exceptional cases can abortions be performed beyond this period. <h2><strong>8. Are There Any Legal Protections for Women Seeking Abortions in India?</strong></h2> Yes, the MTP Act provides legal protections for women seeking abortions in India. The Act ensures that only registered medical practitioners can perform abortions, and it prohibits the disclosure of the woman's identity without her consent. This protects the woman's privacy and ensures that she can access safe and legal abortion services without fear of stigma or legal repercussions. <h2><strong>9. Can a Woman Get an Abortion for Non-Health Reasons in India?</strong></h2> No, a woman cannot get an abortion for non-health reasons in India. The MTP Act allows abortions only under specific health-related grounds, such as risk to physical or mental health, fetal abnormalities, and rape. Abortion on demand is not permitted. <h2><strong>10. How Does India Compare to Other Countries in Terms of Abortion Laws?</strong></h2> India's abortion laws are relatively progressive compared to some countries. The MTP Act allows for abortion under broader grounds than some other countries, including for mental health reasons and in cases of contraceptive failure. However, India's 24-week gestational limit is lower than in some countries, and there are still challenges in ensuring access to safe and legal abortion services.These FAQs provide additional insights into the legalities of abortion in India, highlighting the specific conditions under which abortions are permitted and the legal protections available to women seeking these services. <h2><strong>11. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Incest?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of incest can get an abortion in India. The Medical Termination of Pregnancy (MTP) Act allows for abortion in cases where the pregnancy is a result of rape, which includes incest. This ensures that women who have been subjected to this form of sexual abuse can access safe and legal abortion services. <h2><strong>12. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Trafficking?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of trafficking can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act allows for abortion in cases where the pregnancy is a result of rape, which can include cases of sexual exploitation and trafficking. This provision helps protect the reproductive rights of women who have been subjected to these forms of abuse. <h2><strong>13. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Domestic Violence?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of domestic violence can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act allows for abortion in cases where the continuance of the pregnancy would involve a risk to the life of the pregnant woman or cause grave injury to her physical or mental health. Domestic violence can be considered a factor in determining the risk to the woman's mental health. <h2><strong>14. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Forced Marriage?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of forced marriage can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act allows for abortion in cases where the pregnancy is a result of rape, which can include cases of forced marriage. This provision helps protect the reproductive rights of women who have been subjected to this form of abuse. <h2><strong>15. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Honor Killing?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of honor killing can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act allows for abortion in cases where the continuance of the pregnancy would involve a risk to the life of the pregnant woman or cause grave injury to her physical or mental health. Threats of honor killing can be considered a factor in determining the risk to the woman's mental health. <h2><strong>16. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Female Genital Mutilation?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of female genital mutilation can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act allows for abortion in cases where the continuance of the pregnancy would involve a risk to the life of the pregnant woman or cause grave injury to her physical or mental health. The trauma and health consequences of female genital mutilation can be considered a factor in determining the risk to the woman's mental health. <h2><strong>17. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Acid Attack?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of an acid attack can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act allows for abortion in cases where the continuance of the pregnancy would involve a risk to the life of the pregnant woman or cause grave injury to her physical or mental health. The physical and psychological trauma of an acid attack can be considered a factor in determining the risk to the woman's health. <h2><strong>18. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Child Marriage?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of child marriage can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act allows for abortion in cases where the continuance of the pregnancy would involve a risk to the life of the pregnant woman or cause grave injury to her physical or mental health. The young age and lack of maturity of a child bride can be considered a factor in determining the risk to her health.These additional FAQs highlight the various circumstances under which a woman can access legal and safe abortion services in India, including cases of sexual assault, domestic violence, forced marriage, and other forms of abuse and exploitation. <h2><strong>1. Can a Woman Get an Abortion Without Her Family's Consent?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman can get an abortion without her family's consent. The Medical Termination of Pregnancy (MTP) Act of 1971 only requires the woman's consent, and the consent of family members is not necessary. This ensures that the woman's autonomy and reproductive rights are protected. <h2><strong>2. Can a Woman Get an Abortion After 24 Weeks in India?</strong></h2> No, a woman cannot get an abortion after 24 weeks in India, except in specific cases where a medical board has approved the termination due to substantial fetal abnormalities. The MTP Act sets a 24-week limit for abortions, and only in exceptional cases can abortions be performed beyond this period. <h2><strong>3. Does India Have a Law Against Marital Rape?</strong></h2> No, India does not have a specific law against marital rape. However, the MTP Act allows for abortion in cases of rape, including marital rape. This means that even if marital rape is not criminalized, a woman can still seek an abortion if her pregnancy is a result of rape. <h2><strong>4. Can a Woman Get an Abortion for Non-Health Reasons in India?</strong></h2> No, a woman cannot get an abortion for non-health reasons in India. The MTP Act allows abortions only under specific health-related grounds, such as risk to physical or mental health, fetal abnormalities, and rape. Abortion on demand is not permitted. <h2><strong>5. How Does India Compare to Other Countries in Terms of Abortion Laws?</strong></h2> India's abortion laws are relatively progressive compared to some countries. The MTP Act allows for abortion under broader grounds than some other countries, including for mental health reasons and in cases of contraceptive failure. However, India's 24-week gestational limit is lower than in some countries, and there are still challenges in ensuring access to safe and legal abortion services. <h2><strong>6. Can a Woman Get an Abortion Without Her Spouse's Consent?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman can get an abortion without her spouse's consent. The MTP Act does not require spousal consent for the abortion procedure. This ensures that the woman's right to reproductive autonomy is protected, regardless of her marital status. <h2><strong>7. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Minor?</strong></h2> Yes, a minor girl can get an abortion in India. However, the written consent of her legal guardian is required. The MTP Act allows abortions under certain health-related grounds, which can include the case of a minor girl who is unlikely to be able to raise a child due to her age. <h2><strong>8. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is Unmarried?</strong></h2> Yes, an unmarried woman can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act permits abortion under similar conditions as for married women, such as risk to physical or mental health, fetal abnormalities, and contraceptive failure. However, the consent of a parent or guardian is required if the woman is a minor. <h2><strong>9. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Sexual Assault?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of sexual assault can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act allows for abortion in cases of rape, including marital rape. This means that even if the rape is not reported or not criminalized, a woman can still seek an abortion if her pregnancy is a result of sexual assault. <h2><strong>10. Can a Woman Get an Abortion in India if She Is a Victim of Marital Rape?</strong></h2> Yes, a woman who is a victim of marital rape can get an abortion in India. The MTP Act allows for abortion in cases of rape, which includes marital rape. This means that even if marital rape is not criminalized, a woman can still seek an abortion if her pregnancy is a result of marital rape.These FAQs provide additional insights into the legalities of abortion in India, highlighting the specific conditions under which abortions are permitted and the legal protections available to women seeking these services.|35688|2024-07-25 19:29:04|2024-07-25 13:59:04|closed|closed|is-abortion-legal-in-india|publish|0|0|blog_post||0| | | |_wds_readability|a:4:{s:5:"score";i:56;s:9:"raw_score";i:56;s:11:"is_readable";b:0;s:5:"error";b:0;}| |

| | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | |Varicocele treatment without surgery: Varicocele Embolization| | |Medagg| |Medagg| |<div> <div class="border-borderMain/50 ring-borderMain/50 divide-borderMain/50 dark:divide-borderMainDark/50 dark:ring-borderMainDark/50 dark:border-borderMainDark/50 bg-transparent"> <div class="relative default font-sans text-base text-textMain dark:text-textMainDark selection:bg-super/50 selection:text-textMain dark:selection:bg-superDuper/10 dark:selection:text-superDark"> <div class="min-w-0 break-words [word-break:break-word]"> <div dir="auto"> <div> <div class="prose dark:prose-invert inline leading-normal break-words min-w-0 [word-break:break-word]">Varicocele, a condition marked by enlarged veins in the scrotum, can lead to complications such as infertility if not addressed. Traditionally, surgical options like laparoscopic varicocelectomy have been the standard treatment, but they come with significant risks and recovery times. Fortunately, advancements in medical technology have introduced non-surgical alternatives, such as varicocele embolization. This minimally invasive procedure allows for effective treatment without the need for major incisions, significantly reducing recovery time and minimizing complications. In this article, we will explore the nature of varicocele, traditional treatment methods, and the advantages of choosing embolization as a safer, more efficient option for managing this condition.</div> <div><img class="alignnone wp-image-35693" src="https://medagghealthcare.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/Varicocele-treatment-without-surgery-1024x576.png" alt="Varicocele treatment without surgery" width="1269" height="714" /></div> </div> </div> </div> </div> </div> </div> <h2>What is Varicocele?</h2> A condition that results in a collection of enlarged veins in the Scrotum (<strong>the bag that holds a man's testicles</strong>) is known as <strong>Varicocele</strong>.  Varicocele affects the veins that travel up towards the spermatic cord. The spermatic cord contains the tube that carries sperm from the testes to the penis, lymphatic vessels, and nerves.  A Varicocele if left untreated, might affect the development of the testicles and may result in decreased sperm count leading to infertility. <h2><strong>Understanding A Varicocele</strong></h2> <h3>Definition of the Condition:</h3> Varicocele is a swelling of the veins in the scrotum that usually happens when the valves in these veins fail, resulting in the blood to back up and pool.  Although there is no specific reason that causes this condition, experts say that these might contribute to resulting in a Varicocele.  <img src="https://images.surferseo.art/26a386e6-faf5-41c7-8217-b8bce4d39340.jpeg" /> <h4>Hormonal Changes:</h4> During puberty the testicles grow quickly and usually require more blood than normal. But if the valves in the scrotum don't function properly the veins won't be able to handle the extra flow of blood and causes it to pool up. This ultimately might be a key reason that can cause a Varicocele. <h4>Defective Valves:</h4> The valves in the veins are responsible for redirecting blood flow, so in case the valves in the veins of the scrotum don't function as usual then it causes the blood to accumulate in the same place causing swelling and Varicocele formation. <h4>Blood Flow:</h4> Generally, the left side of the testicular veins follow a different pathway than the right. Blood flow on the left side of the testicles is also greater than the right, which can result in a Varicocele. <h2><strong>Traditional Treatments for Varicocele</strong></h2> <h3>Laparoscopic Varicocelectomy:</h3> <strong>Laparoscopic Varicocelectomy</strong> is an open surgery to treat <strong>Varicocele</strong> that involves making major incisions in the abdomen or groin. The procedure involves physically cutting the swollen veins and then closing the ends off. The incisions made in the abdomen or even the groin is closed with stitches or staples. <h3>Risks associated with Laparoscopic Varicocelectomy:</h3> Laparoscopic Varicocelectomy is an open surgery which means the risks associated with it are relatively high. As a matter of fact, in any open surgery the chances of failures or even complications are on the upper side.  But, for a surgery such as a <strong>Laparoscopic Varicocelectomy</strong> which is performed in a very sensitive organ like the <strong>Scrotum</strong>, risks involved shoot up furthermore. Some of them are listed below <ul>  	<li>Excessive Bleeding</li>  	<li>Blood Clots</li>  	<li>Severe infection</li>  	<li>Fluid formation around the testicles (Hydrocele)</li>  	<li>Scarring</li>  	<li>Decrease in Sperm Count</li> </ul> <h2>Varicocele treatment without surgery</h2> With centuries worth of knowledge combined with advancement in technology and medicine, today there are multiple non-surgical solutions to various ailments and diseases that the common man is unaware of.  For a condition such as a Varicocele, <strong>Embolization</strong> is perhaps the most well-known <strong>non-surgical</strong> treatment option that is available.  In this procedure, an <strong>interventional radiologist</strong> uses a coil or special agents to block or embolize the affected veins. This can then improve the overall symptoms. <h2><strong>What is Varicocele Embolization?</strong></h2> <strong>Varicocele Embolization</strong> is a procedure that involves redirecting blood away from an enlarged vein in the scrotum. A radiologist uses a coil or special agents to block or embolize the vein which reduces the swelling and allows the blood to flow without causing it to pool up.  Varicocele Embolization is also a <strong>minimally invasive technique</strong> with no major cuts or incisions involved. <h3><strong>Advantages of Varicocele Embolization Over Traditional Surgery</strong></h3> <h4>Minimally Invasive in Nature:</h4> Compared to other surgical procedures available for Varicocele, Varicocele Embolization is a minimally invasive technique which means that it involves no major incisions or cuts to be performed. <h4>Faster Recovery:</h4> Varicocele Embolization allows the patient to recover in a very short span of time. An open surgery involves the doctor to make major cuts or incisions on the patient which takes a lot of time to heal and recover.  Since this procedure is a minimally invasive technique which does not involve major incisions or even cuts, the patient usually recovers from the procedure in no time. <h2><strong>What happens in the Process of Varicocele Embolization?</strong></h2> <h3>Pre-procedure preparation</h3> First, you’ll be given medicine to make you feel comfortable, relaxed and sleepy. The area where the procedure is to be performed will be cleansed to avoid any sort of infection.  A small incision is made through the inner part of the upper thigh and a Catheter is sent through. A Catheter is a thin, flexible tube used to carry micro particles or special agents.  One of the major veins is accessed through this small incision and with the help of x-rays an <strong>interventional radiologist</strong> will move the tube to the correct area in your scrotum and then a small coil or a special liquid will be inserted into the affected vein.  This is called a blocking agent. This redirects the blood flow into other nearby veins and helps the blood to exit the scrotum normally.  After the procedure the catheter will be removed, and a bandage will be placed on the area of entry on your thigh. <h3>Post-procedure care and recovery</h3> This technique is a <strong>Day Care Procedure</strong>, in other words it does not require the patient to get admitted for days and allows them to get discharged as soon as the treatment is over.  Also, since the procedure is minimally invasive, the patient can get back to resuming normal activities in a couple of days. As mentioned, the recovery time span for patients undergoing this procedure is very less when compared to other surgical alternatives. <h3><strong>Why Varicocele Embolization is the Best Varicocele Treatment?</strong></h3> Varicocele Embolization is a non-surgical treatment option to treat Varicocele. It is a minimally invasive technique unlike others surgical treatment options available for this condition.  The most important aspect of this procedure is that it provides the patient the ability to recover quickly. It is a day care procedure which means that the patient can go home the same day.  The procedure does not involve any scarring or suture and all it does is redirects the blood flow in the veins of the scrotum and thereby reduces swelling, removes blood clot and provides permanent relief from other symptoms of Varicocele.  For these reasons it is considered one of the most advanced and safest procedures when compared to its surgical counterparts. <h3><strong>Varicocele treatment without surgery: Step-by-Step Guide</strong></h3> The first and foremost thing to do when you feel you have most of the symptoms that relate to Varicocele, is to consult a Urologist. <h4>Here is a Step-to-Step Guide of the Treatment:</h4> <h4>Determining if you are Diagnosed with a Varicocele</h4> A Urologist will help you determine if the condition you are dealing with is actually Varicocele. Sometimes the symptoms might overlap with other conditions, and you might end up not even having Varicocele. <h4>Monitoring and Observing</h4> In some cases, the intensity of Varicocele might not be life threatening and in such instances, doctors recommend patients to be on regular checkups. This might require the patient to follow up on a habitual basis to ensure the condition doesn't worsen. <h4>Varicocele Embolization</h4> The procedure is usually performed by an interventional radiologist. A small incision is made on the upper part of the inner thigh to insert a tube called a Catheter. This tube carries microparticles and can access the testicular veins in the Scrotum.  The microparticles embolize or redirect the blood flow to a healthier vein which relieves the blood clot and swelling.  Once the procedure is done, the tube also known as the Catheter carrying the microparticles is drawn back out via the same route. The small incision is then sealed off using a bandage. <h4>Relief and Recovery</h4> Varicocele treatment without surgery can truly be a blessing. Imagine having multiple stitches on the Scrotum, one of the most sensitive organs in a man. Varicocele Embolization on the other hand provides room for a quicker, safer and relaxed recovery.  This technique is also a day care procedure and does not require the patient to get admitted for days. <h3>Importance of choosing the right specialist</h3> Options and choices are limitless in today’s world, from the food we consume to fashion, we never fail to compare and differentiate alternatives before taking a final call.  Given the choices available in almost all sectors of life, we are still hesitant to choose wisely when it comes to the most important aspect, health.  Why choose a single healthcare provider when we can bring you a multitude of options with neutrality inbuilt.  At Medagg we help you choose the ‘right treatment’ and the ‘right hospital’. <h2>Common questions and Expert answers:</h2> <h3>1. How do you diagnose Varicocele?</h3> A scrotal ultrasonography is performed in conjunction with a physical examination to diagnose varicoceles. <h3>2. Can an infertile person get Varicoceles?</h3> Indeed, varicoceles can impact sperm production and quality, which in some cases could result in infertility. <h3>3. Can Varicoceles reoccur after getting treated?</h3> Despite the fact that varicocele treatment generally is successful, there is a small chance that it might reoccur in some circumstances. <h3>4. How much time does it take to recover from the treatment?</h3> Recovery periods can vary, but depending on the type of treatment, many patients can return to their regular activities in a few days. <h3>5. Is it possible to avoid varicoceles?</h3> Since varicoceles frequently arise naturally, they cannot be prevented. | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | |How Many Days of Bleeding After Abortion: Is abortion painful?| | |Medagg| |Medagg| |<img class="alignnone" src="https://images.surferseo.art/c598c52e-9d6a-4ccb-a0a2-351bd2c0a637.png" alt="how many days bleed after abortion " width="1120" height="630" />  Medical Termination of Pregnancy (<strong>MTP</strong>) is a procedure used to end a pregnancy using medication in the form of pills. This method is commonly used in the early stages of pregnancy usually up to 10 weeks of gestation. <strong>Medical Termination of Pregnancy</strong> is highly effective and considered one of the most safest and risk free procedure as it bears no threats to future pregnancies. <strong>98 % </strong>percent of the time medical termination of pregnancy is extremely efficient and yields desired results. <h2><strong>Types of Abortion</strong></h2> <h3><strong>1. Medical Abortion</strong></h3> <strong>MTP </strong>is the non surgical solution to abortion. <strong>Medical Termination of Pregnancy </strong>involves taking medication in the form of pills which blocks the effect of progesterone, the hormone needed for the pregnancy to continue.  <strong>Mifepristone</strong>: This medication is taken first, usually at a healthcare provider's clinic. Mifepristone blocks the hormone progesterone, which is necessary for the pregnancy to continue.  <strong>Misoprostol</strong>: This medication is taken 24 to 48 hours after the Mifepristone. Misoprostol causes the uterus to contract, leading to the expulsion of the pregnancy tissue.  The medical abortion process typically takes place over few days, with the patient taking the medications and experiencing the abortion at home. <h3><strong>2. Surgical Abortion</strong></h3> <img src="https://images.surferseo.art/d7e93a93-956c-4b35-b858-662a65773161.jpeg" />  Procedures such as the <strong>D and C technique</strong> which can be performed during the first trimester. During the procedure the doctor dilates the cervix with an instrument or medication, then scrapes the uterine lining with a <strong>spoon shaped instrument called a curette</strong> to remove existing tissue.  <strong>D and E Abortion</strong> (<strong>Dilation and Evacuation Abortion</strong>), is another technique which is usually performed in the Second Trimester (mostly after 13 weeks of pregnancy )  The procedure is performed by dilating the cervix (<strong>the passage that connects the uterus and the vagina </strong>) which is followed by the suction method. <h2><strong>What is Surgical Termination Of Pregnancy (STP)?</strong></h2> <strong>Surgical Termination of Pregnancy</strong> is a surgical procedure used to terminate a pregnancy. <strong>STP</strong> is performed in two ways namely, <strong>D and C (Dilation and Curettage) Abortion</strong> and <strong>Dilation and Evacuation Abortion</strong> (D&amp;E Abortion).  <strong>a. D and C (Dilation and Curettage) </strong>Abortion  Dilation and Curettage Abortion is a surgical technique which is performed during the first trimester of pregnancy. During this procedure the doctor dilates the cervix with an instrument or medication, then scrapes the uterine lining with a <strong>curette </strong>(a spoon shaped instrument) to remove existing Fetal tissue.  <strong>b. Dilation and Evacuation Abortion</strong> (D&amp;E Abortion) :  Dilation and Evacuation Abortion is a surgical procedure used to terminate pregnancy primarily during the second trimester.  The procedure involves dilating the cervix and then using a suction instrument to remove the foetus and the placenta. However, when compared to <strong>D and C Abortion </strong>, <strong>Dilation and Evacuation Abortion</strong> (D and E Abortion) is a bit more complex to perform. <h2>Aftercare and Recovery</h2> Recovery phase is as important as choosing which type of procedure you are opting for. Whether you choose surgical or non surgical abortion, giving yourself time and making yourself comfortable during the entire process is crucial.  Here are some key points to consider : <h3>Bleeding and Cramping</h3> &nbsp;  <img src="https://images.surferseo.art/0f273981-efa6-4491-9d37-11a6990d84cd.png" alt="Bleeding and Cramping" />  <strong>Bleeding</strong> is a common symptom post abortion and lasts on an average of about a week or so, depending on the individual and the chosen type of abortion. You may experience varying levels of bleeding and cramping, depending on the type of abortion and your individual response. If you are experiencing extreme bleeding for more than a day or two it is highly recommended to consult a health professional.  <strong>Medical abortion:</strong> Moderate bleeding and cramping are typical, as the uterus contracts to expel the pregnancy tissue.  <strong>Surgical abortion:</strong> Lighter bleeding and cramping are noticed, as the pregnancy tissue is removed directly. However, risk factors including in procedure complications are relatively higher.  After your abortion, it is important to discuss birth control options with your healthcare provider to prevent an unintended pregnancy. <h2><strong>How soon after an abortion can you get pregnant?</strong></h2> A previous abortion does not affect the chances of a woman getting pregnant again nor does it affect her future pregnancies. Once the ovulation cycle starts which can be as early as 2 weeks, chances of the woman conceiving are back to normal. <h2><strong>How to remove retained products of conception after abortion?</strong></h2> In rare cases, some pregnancy tissue may remain in the uterus after an abortion. This is known as retained products of conception. If you experience prolonged bleeding or severe cramping, contact your healthcare provider, who may recommend a follow-up procedure to remove any of the remaining tissue. <h2><strong>Is Abortion Painful?</strong></h2> The experience of pain during an abortion varies from person to person and depends on the type of abortion procedure. Here’s what you can generally expect: <h3>Medical Abortion:</h3> <ul>  	<li><strong>Pain Level:</strong> Often described as similar to heavy menstrual cramps.</li>  	<li><strong>Duration:</strong> Pain typically starts within a few hours of taking the medication and can last for a few days.</li>  	<li><strong>Management:</strong> Over-the-counter pain relievers and prescribed medications can help manage discomfort.</li> </ul> <h3>Surgical Abortion:</h3> <ul>  	<li><strong>Pain Level:</strong> Some people experience cramping during and after the procedure.</li>  	<li><strong>Duration:</strong> Pain is usually brief during the procedure and may continue for a few hours afterward.</li>  	<li><strong>Management:</strong> Local anesthesia, sedation, or general anesthesia are used to minimize pain during the procedure. Pain relievers can be used after the procedure.</li> </ul> <h3>Emotional Experience:</h3> <ul>  	<li><strong>Emotional Pain:</strong> It's normal to have a range of emotions after an abortion, from relief to sadness. Support from friends, family, or a counselor can be helpful.</li> </ul> <h2><strong>How to stop bleeding after abortion?</strong></h2> Understanding what to expect in terms of bleeding and recovery can help you manage the process more effectively.  To manage bleeding after an abortion, follow these steps: <ol>  	<li><strong>Rest</strong>: Take it slow for a few days, allow your body to completely recover from the process.</li>  	<li><strong>Pain Relief</strong>: Pain relievers like ibuprofen or paracetamol can be used to manage cramping and discomfort. Consult a health professional before proceeding further.</li>  	<li><strong>Bleeding Management</strong>: Use sanitary pads rather than tampons until the bleeding stops. Avoid using tampons during the abortion process to prevent infection.</li> </ol> <h2><strong>How Long After Abortion Do Symptoms of Pregnancy Go Away?</strong></h2> After an abortion, the symptoms of pregnancy will gradually diminish. Here's a general timeline of what to expect: <h4>Immediate Changes:</h4> <ul>  	<li><strong>Within a Few Days:</strong> <ul>  	<li><strong>Nausea:</strong> Pregnancy-related nausea usually starts to improve within a few days after the abortion.</li>  	<li><strong>Breast Tenderness:</strong> Breast soreness and tenderness often begin to decrease within a few days to a week.</li> </ul> </li> </ul> <h4>Short-Term Changes:</h4> <ul>  	<li><strong>Within 1-2 Weeks:</strong> <ul>  	<li><strong>Fatigue:</strong> You may feel less tired as your hormone levels start to return to normal.</li>  	<li><strong>Frequent Urination:</strong> This symptom usually resolves as your body readjusts.</li> </ul> </li> </ul> <h4>Longer-Term Changes:</h4> <ul>  	<li><strong>Within 4-6 Weeks:</strong> <ul>  	<li><strong>Hormonal Adjustment:</strong> It can take several weeks for pregnancy hormones (hCG) to completely leave your body.</li>  	<li><strong>Menstrual Cycle:</strong> Your regular menstrual cycle should resume within 4-6 weeks, though this can vary from person to person.</li> </ul> </li> </ul> <h2><strong>Conclusion</strong></h2> Abortion is a safe and legal medical procedure that can be performed using either medical or surgical methods. Proper aftercare is crucial to ensure a smooth recovery. If you're considering an abortion, consult a certified healthcare provider and follow their instructions to minimize risks and maximize comfort. <h2><strong>Frequently Asked Questions :</strong></h2> <h3>1. How does abortion bleeding look like?</h3> Bleeding after an abortion can vary in amount and duration. It may be heavier than a normal period, with clots and tissue passing. The bleeding can be intermittent, stopping and starting all over again. Not to worry this is the natural process of the body trying to expel the pregnancy to bring back the uterus to it's initial state. <h3>2. How many days to get periods after an abortion?</h3> You can typically expect your period to return within 4-6 weeks after an abortion. However, it may take longer, up to 8-12 weeks in some cases, depending on the individual and chosen type of abortion. <h3>3. Why am I still bleeding 8 weeks after an abortion?</h3> Prolonged bleeding beyond 6 weeks may be a sign of retained pregnancy tissue or other complications. You should consult your healthcare provider immediately if the bleeding persists for more than 6 weeks. <h3>4. What can cause no period after an abortion?</h3> Lack of a period after an abortion can be caused by hormonal changes, stress, or other medical conditions. If you don't get your period within 8-12 weeks, you should see your doctor. <h3>5. How long after a miscarriage or abortion can you get pregnant?</h3> You can get pregnant as soon as 2 weeks after an abortion or miscarriage, so it's important to use contraception if you don't want to get pregnant again right away. <h3>6. Will I be able to conceive after an abortion?</h3> In most cases, having an abortion does not affect future fertility, and you should be able to conceive again after your next normal menstrual cycle. <h3>7. Is it easier to get pregnant after a miscarriage?</h3> There is some evidence that fertility may temporarily increase after a miscarriage, but this is not a guarantee. Your chances of conceiving will depend on various factors. <h3>8. How many days bleed after abortion ?</h3> The duration and intensity of bleeding after an abortion can vary depending on the type of procedure and individual factors. Incase of medical abortion bleeding typically starts within hours of taking the medication and can last for 1 to 2 weeks. Some light spotting may continue for a few weeks after that. Bleeding after a surgical abortion generally lasts for 1 to 2 weeks. Some women may experience light spotting for a few additional weeks <h4></h4>|35699|2024-08-01 18:55:49|2024-08-01 13:25:49|closed|closed|how-many-days-bleed-after-abortion|publish|0|0|blog_post||0| | | |_wds_readability|a:4:{s:5:"score";i:56;s:9:"raw_score";i:56;s:11:"is_readable";b:0;s:5:"error";b:0;}| |

| | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | |Can Enlarged Prostate be Cured Without Surgery?| | |Medagg| |Medagg| |<h3><strong><img class="alignnone wp-image-35703" src="https://medagghealthcare.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/Treating-enlarged-prostate-be-cured-without-surgery-1-1024x576.png" alt="Treating enlarged prostate be cured without surgery (1)" width="1273" height="716" /></strong></h3> <h2>What is Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia (BPH)?</h2> A condition that results in enlarged prostate is referred to as Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia (BPH). The prostate gland contributes to the production of sperm in men, and it is fairly common for the prostate gland to grow larger as one gets older.  An enlarged prostate is not something that should cause you a great deal of anxiety, but at the same time if you do nothing about it, it could trigger issues in a number of different ways.  For Example, obstructions in urine flow down the bladder, discomfort in the urinary tract, and kidney difficulties.  <img class="" src="https://images.surferseo.art/c173240b-13fd-40e2-8372-0c939a234ad3.jpeg" width="1272" height="836" /> <h2>What Causes an Enlarged Prostate?</h2> <img class="alignleft" src="https://images.surferseo.art/0e512405-c17b-4570-92cb-585cbfe26ebf.jpeg" />  Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia is influenced by a number of circumstances however, the precise cause of the condition is not completely understood. The chief contributors to Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia (BPH) in men are: <h3><strong>Hormonal Changes Associated with Aging</strong></h3> As men get older, their testosterone levels continue to fall, while their estrogen scale either remain the same or increase. An imbalance in hormones is thought to be the primary contributing factor in the growth of the prostate. <h4><strong>Dihydrotestosterone, also known as DHT </strong></h4> A significant role for the formation and growth of your prostate gland is played by this testosterone derivative. The accumulation of increased levels of DHT of prostate, which can lead to enlargement, is more likely to occur in older men. <h3><strong>Lifestyle and Health </strong></h3> Excessive body weight can have an effect on hormone levels and contribute to the enlargement of the prostate for people who are obese.  An insufficient amount of physical activity has been associated with an increased risk for benign prostatic hyperplasia (BPH). <h3><strong>Diabetes</strong></h3> Men with diabetes have an increased chance of developing benign prostatic hyperplasia (BPH). Cardiovascular Health is connected to the health of the prostate, and there is a correlation between the two, according to specific research. <h2>Symptoms of Enlargement of the Prostate</h2> BPH, also known as <strong>benign prostatic hyperplasia</strong>, is a condition that usually affects men as they get older. It is characterized by an enlarged prostate.  The prostate gland, which is located below the bladder results in the urethra to enlarge, which can cause a variety of urinary symptoms as well as other health problems.  For efficient management of Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia, it is essential to have a solid understanding of BPH's symptoms and how they affect one's day-to-day life. <h4>Difficulty with Urine Flow</h4> If you are suffering with Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia, you would often experience difficulty in starting urination and finally emptying your bladder. This occurs because the enlarged prostate compresses the urethra and makes it harder for urine to flow completely out the bladder. <h4>Weak Urine Flow</h4> The most common symptom of Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia is a noticeable decrease in the strength and volume of the urine stream. Because of an enlarged prostate the urethra narrows down in size and restricts urine flow, leading to a weak stream. <h4>Urgency to Urinate</h4> Patients with an enlarged prostate sometimes get a sudden, strong urge to urinate which can cause difficulty in delaying urination. This urgency can lead to situations were finding a restroom quickly becomes a priority. <h4>Frequent Urination</h4> An enlarged prostate gland can cause an increase in the need to urinate, especially during the night (<strong>nocturia</strong>). This can significantly disrupt sleep patterns and daily activities. <h3>Effects of BPH on daily life</h3> <h4>Disturbed Sleep</h4> For patients with Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia, it is possible for them to have a disturbed sleep routine because of frequent urination during the night. This insufficient amount of sleep can result in feelings of exhaustion, lower attention, and a general drop in productivity throughout the day. <h4><strong>Reduced Physical Activity</strong></h4> Men with suffering with Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia can be demotivated from participating in activities when there is restricted access to restrooms due to the urgency and frequency of urine flow.  This might result in a lifestyle that is defined as sedentary, which in turn can have an impact on one's general health and fitness. <h4>Stress and Anxiety</h4> The constant need to be near a restroom can cause significant stress and anxiety. Men with BPH symptoms may worry about embarrassing accidents or being in situations where they cannot easily access a restroom. <h4>Professional Challenges</h4> The enlargement of the prostate can cause the need for frequent bathroom breaks and can affect work performance and decrease productivity.  Men may feel self-conscious about their condition, leading to decreased confidence in professional settings as well. <h2><strong>Traditional Treatments options for Enlarged Prostate</strong></h2> <h3>TURP (Transurethral Resection of the Prostate)</h3> TURP, which stands for <strong>transurethral resection of the prostate</strong>, is a surgical procedure that is used to treat patients suffering with BPH symptoms, which is a condition that is characterized by an enlarged prostate gland.  For <strong>surgical treatment</strong> of BPH, TURP is the go-to option, but has its own downsides as well.  This procedure is carried out with the use of a resectoscope, which is an instrument that is introduced into the urethra through the tip of the penis.  The resectoscope is equipped with a light, valves that allow the irrigating fluid to be controlled, and an electrical loop that facilitates the cutting of prostate tissue and then sealing of blood arteries. <h3>Risks and Side Effects of Transurethral resection of the Prostate (TURP)</h3> When compared to other surgical procedures risks associated with TURP (Transurethral Resection of the prostate) is comparatively high since it's performed on a highly sensitive organ such as the penis.  Some of the possible complications include: <h4>Excessive Bleeding</h4> Bleeding during and after the procedure is quite common. But in rare cases, significant bleeding may require a complete blood transfusion. <h4>Infection</h4> There is a risk of infection at the surgical site or in the urinary tract. Antibiotics are often prescribed to prevent infections and further complications. <h4><strong>Retrograde Ejaculation</strong></h4> Is when your semen flows backward into the bladder instead of out through the penis during ejaculation and is a common side effect. This can have a severe effect on fertility outcomes too. <h4><strong>Urethral Stricture</strong></h4> Scarring of your urethra during the procedure, can lead to narrowing and blockage, requiring further treatment. <h2><strong>Enlarged Prostate Treatment without Surgery</strong></h2> <h3>Non-Surgical Solution to treat an Enlarged Prostate</h3> With Centuries worth of knowledge combines with advancements in technology and medicine, today there are multiple non-surgical solutions to various ailments and diseases that the common man in unaware of.  One such solution to treat an enlargement in the prostate gland is <strong>PAE (Prostate Artery Embolization)</strong> <h3>Benefits of Non-Surgical Treatments</h3> <h4>Minimally Invasive</h4> Non-Surgical techniques do not involve large incisions, cuts to be made during the procedures which is a huge advantage over traditional surgeries.  Since they are highly advanced treatments, latest methods like using a catheter to treat ailments along with imaging techniques provide the patient with minimal scarring and a faster recovery phase. These procedures are usually performed by an interventional radiologist. <h4>Day Care Procedures</h4> Non-surgical solutions do not require the patients to get admitted for days to the hospital. In most cases, the patient can return home the very same day.  They can also continue with their regular activities within a few days. <h4>Minimal Side Effects</h4> When compared to traditional surgical methods which usually involve open surgeries, non-surgical solutions have minimal side effects on the body. <h2><strong>What is Prostate Artery Embolization (PAE) for Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia?</strong></h2> <img src="https://images.surferseo.art/874534df-92ca-44aa-adbe-12b80c58abec.jpeg" />  Prostate Artery Embolization is an innovative technique used to treat an enlarged prostate with minimal post-effects on the body.  Usually, PAE is performed by an interventional radiologist by releasing microscopic particles into the arteries that feed the prostate gland. These particles block the blood that flows into the gland and then with time, the size of your prostate decreases.  While other treatments show an alarming impact on men’s health in general, PAE involves low risks and anyone who undergoes this procedure can return back to their normal routine within a couple of days. <h2>How PAE (Prostate Artery Embolization) helps treat an enlarged prostate?</h2> The procedure involves placing a tiny catheter into the arteries that supply blood to the prostate gland. A solution containing thousands of microscopic plastic beads is injected, which in turn blocks the blood flow to the gland. This is done through a small hole that is pierced through the groin.  General anesthesia is not required since the pain is almost unrecognizable, and the patients are discharged during the same course of the day.  With time the prostate gland decreases in size since it is deprived of its blood supply. And thereby the urethra opens for urine to flow normally.  The procedure does not have any negative effect on one’s sexual function and on the contrary a small percentage of patients have experienced an improvement in their overall sexual function <h3><strong>Advantages of Prostate Artery Embolization Over TURP </strong></h3> <h4>Minimally invasive in nature</h4> Prostate Artery Embolization is a minimally invasive technique which does not involve any large incisions to be made. <h4>Faster Recovery</h4> Since the procedure is minimally invasive and a non-surgical technique, it provides the patient to recover swiftly when compared other traditional surgical alternatives. <h4>Lower risk of complications</h4> Prostate Artery Embolization being a non-surgical solution to treat Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia, reduces the risk of complications significantly since it does not involve major cuts, incisions to be made. <h4>Preservation of Sexual function and Urinary control</h4> The procedure does not have any negative effect on one’s sexual function and on the contrary a small percentage of patients have experienced an improvement in their overall sexual function and urinary control. <h2>When to See a Doctor for Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia?</h2> BPH, also known as benign prostatic hyperplasia, is a condition that is rather common, particularly in men who are older in age. It is defined by the expansion and enlargement of the prostate gland. While BPH itself is not cancerous, it can cause uncomfortable urinary symptoms that significantly affect the quality of life.  In order to effectively manage this condition, it is crucial to be aware of when it is necessary to seek medical assistance. <h3><strong>Frequent Urination</strong></h3> If you find out that you need to urinate more frequently than normal, especially during the night (<strong>also known as nocturia</strong>), it may be time to make an appointment with a medical professional. <h3><strong>Urgency</strong></h3> A sudden and pressing need to urinate that is impossible to postpone can be an indication that there is a problem within the body.  When you detect a noticeable decrease in the strength and volume of your urine stream, this may be a sign that you have BPH. <h3><strong>Difficulty Beginning Urination</strong></h3> Being hesitant or having to exert effort in order to start urinating is a typical symptom that should be evaluated by a medical professional. <h3><strong>Interrupted Urine Flow </strong></h3> If your urine stream gets interrupted and starts and stops at random intervals, this could be an indication of an obstruction that is produced by an enlarged prostate. <h3><strong>Incomplete Bladder Emptying</strong></h3> If you continuously get the sensation that your bladder is not totally empty after you have finished urinating, you should consider visiting a healthcare professional. <h3><strong>Painful Urination</strong></h3> If you experience pain or discomfort while urinating, this may be a sign of benign prostatic hyperplasia, and it is important to get checked. <h3><strong>Blood in Urine</strong></h3> <strong>Hematuria</strong>, also known as blood in the urine, is a significant symptom that need to be treated by a medical professional as soon as possible. <h2><strong>FAQ's About Prostate Artery Embolization</strong></h2> <h3>1. Who is a suitable candidate for PAE?</h3> PAE is for men with an enlarged prostate and men who experience urinary flow problems. Also, for people who have not responded well to medications and wish to avoid traditional surgical treatments like TURP. <h3>2. Is PAE a permanent solution for enlarged prostate?</h3> PAE can provide long-lasting relief from urinary symptoms associated with enlarged prostate along with improved sexual function as well. <h3>3. What is the recovery time after Prostate Artery Embolization?</h3> Patients can return to their regular activities within a few days after PAE, with minimal discomfort and shorter recovery compared to traditional surgeries like TURP.|35705|2024-08-12 11:36:42|2024-08-12 06:06:42|closed|closed|can-enlarged-prostate-be-cured-without-surgery|publish|0|0|blog_post||0|post_tag|prostate|prostate|_wds_readability|a:4:{s:5:"score";i:46;s:9:"raw_score";i:46;s:11:"is_readable";b:0;s:5:"error";b:0;}| |
